<GmapID>0x80914302885df2bf:0x491328f9e79e738a<//GmapID><text>I want to preface this with two things. My reviews and pics on google maps are about 99% positive and they have over 5,000,000 hits. Second, I've purchased/owned over 15 bikes during my lifetime and currently own a BMW K1600 Grand America, which is not an inexpensive bike. I called Merced Powersports looking for a Honda Rebel 300 or 500 for my fiancee who had just passed her bike safety class at the old Castle Air Force Base. This was to be her first motorcycle purchase. I spoke to Jordan who told me they had a 2021 Rebel 500 in black and quoted me $6399. He said he was not in sales so Josh, the sales manager would have to help me when I came in. We arrived at the store and asked for Josh. Josh told us that Jordan should not have quoted because he is not in sales. The price turned out to be a few hundred more than what I was told on the phone. 1st "MISTAKE." After my fiancee was comfortable that she wanted to buy, Josh gave us an out the door price and we asked to start the bike to hear it. Josh said it wasn't set up yet and we could hear after the paperwork. 2nd "MISTAKE." who puts a vehicle on the floor when a customer can't even start it? Next, the first document he produced stated 2020 Rebel 300. I asked  Josh why. He said the factory sent it to him that way and he would have to change it manually. If I had not caught that can you imagine the nightmare when DMV got a hold of it? 3rd "MISTAKE." After completing the paperwork and paying cash, we went to lunch while they set the bike up. Upon delivery, there was ZERO new owner orientation and ZERO warranty explanation. 4th "MISTAKE." I asked about the owners manual and the rest of the books. Josh said they were normally under the seat but he would check. He never checked under the seat which pretty much indicated he knew damn well they weren't there. 5th MISTAKE. He reappeared with a 2020 manual, not a 2021 and no warranty booklet or owner's card which is supposed to be delivered with the new bike. His excuse....that's what the factory sent with the bike. 6th MISTAKE. He obviously thought we were idiots and thought he could just point to the factory for all his issues. At that point I was done. I filed a case with Honda corporate to obtain the books. They referred Josh to me to resolve my case. Josh called me and during the discussion told me that a real motorcycle owner would not care about the year difference in the manuals because the text is the same. To have this kid insult me in that manner (real motorcyclist) on top of all the bulls*&ing he did was unbelievable. I probably owned 5 bikes before he was a twinkle in his Mama's eye. He told me that he would check on getting the correct books and get back to me. that was on Tuesday and I'm writing this on Thursday. Crickets from Merced Powersports. No follow up call to let me know the status...nothing. What an absolutely disappointing first buying experience for my fiancee. I cannot recommend this dealership to anyone. If I dug a little further, I would expect to find out that Josh is related to the owner. That would be the only way he would be able to keep his position after being on the receiving end of his customer service. I guess they have done so much business throughout covid they can blow off customers like this. If the owners are reading this review, please take heed because there is some serious long term damage being done to your dealership. <user>102581217524052785075</user><name>Kevin Vieira</name><date>1448337844348<//date><Rate>1</Rate><review>The guy in parts was knowledgeable and helpful. Don't take your bike in for service though. I dropped it off early(Sept 18) because they suggested it in case there was an opening before my Oct 10 appointment. I asked them to do one of their service packages, balance my back tire, replace my front tire, and replace my front brake spring (i provided a new one). On Oct 20 they told me the back wheel was bad and they would look for a replacement. I found one myself I let them know and they said they would throw it on there the day I bring it in for me. A week after dropping it off, I called to find out the status and they said to come get it. On November 11, I went in paid for the services and was ready to take it home. I then noticed a hole in my seat and a crack on the side cover. They said they'd "make it right," but suggested I go ahead and take it home. They never admitted nor denied they were responsible for the damage. The also never replaced the front brake return spring because the mechanic said the original part was fine. I told him it was not, and explained the issue. He said I was right and tired to quickly put the new spring on. I left it with them because I didn't want to be somehow blamed for the damages. A week and a half later I call in to find out the status and I was told it was ready for pick up, and the young gentleman in service said they fired the mechanic who worked on my bike. I went the next day to pick it up, the seat was re-upholstered but nothing was done about the crack in the side cover. Chuck told me he was not going to cover the side cover because he "spent $75 to fix the seat and I'm not about to pay $300 for a side cover." He then told me it has scratches and cracks all up and down the cover, so he wasn't about to give me a new one. Yes there were scratches, but there were no cracks because I work on the bike myself and I always examine that I put things back right. I took my key and they told me to take my bike, which was squeezed in next to other bikes, so I asked them to move it because I didn't want to knock down any of the other bikes. I got a dirty look from a sales guy, then the mechanic who worked on my bike (who they claimed had been fired) met me outside to move my bike for me. < text>
Shoreline sober living provided me the guidance, support and structure I needed in early recovery.  After completing treatment, my counselors strongly advised that I attend Shoreline sober living.  Now, after several years of sobriety, I am grateful that I followed that recommendation. My time at Shoreline was the single greatest contributing factor in my path to becoming a highly productive, sober member of society.  I now work in recovery as counselor, which has given me an insider‚Äôs perspective on how Shoreline compares to other sober living programs, and as a result, my appreciation for this program has only grown. The structure of Shoreline‚Äôs program is not like any other you will find in the area. What separates Shoreline from other homes is the culture of comradery, and even more importantly, the level of accountability. Upon entering Shoreline I was accepted with open arms and the residents integrated me into the community quickly- showing me the ins and outs of the daily routines, the best meetings to attend and setting me up with a solid sponsor.  I was also introduced by my fellow residents to many people in the recovery community outside of Shoreline that I now consider friends. I saw this process repeated with each new resident.  Looking back now, I realize how imperative this experience was to my recovery.  Finding and becoming part of a sober community is of paramount importance and Shoreline facilitates this experience in a way that other recovery homes don‚Äôt. Aaron, the Program Manager, does a great job of fostering a positive atmosphere while stressing the importance of a balanced life that includes work, fellowship, commitment, goal setting, financial responsibility and community.  The entire staff, from the top down, genuinely care about helping each resident find success in sobriety and they work closely with each resident to assist in the transition from treatment back into the stream of life. Shoreline‚Äôs location couldn‚Äôt be better since Encinitas is home to an active, robust recovery community.  The houses are centrally located and close to the beach. There is plenty of opportunity for employment in the surrounding area and the houses are walking distance to the gym and shopping centers.  The houses themselves are immaculate and kept clean. I am eternally grateful for the experience I received at Shoreline, and highly recommend this program to anyone looking to find lasting recovery.<//text>

<review>Our son is in his third year of recovery.  We attribute much of his success in now being free from not only drugs but also alcohol and tobacco to the support, care and guidance he received at Shoreline and from its management team. Following a lengthy, 120 day stay at a local San Diego County inpatient treatment facility, he stayed at Shoreline for over a year and since then has maintained contact with the community.  Throughout his stay we were most appreciative of Shoreline's continual weekly progress calls, advice, expertise on addiction and desire to help not only our son, but also all of our family navigate the difficulties that arise throughout the different stages of getting free of intoxicating substances. During his three prior unsuccessful attempts to become free of drug use at nationally known inpatient treatment centers, we never fully understood, nor was there much attempt made by those facilities to make us aware of the critical role a sober living facility and ongoing outpatient treatment provides in achieving lasting recovery. Thirty days of inpatient treatment followed by nothing more than AA meetings and good intentions was a recipe for relapse. During his last in-patient recovery at a well known facility here in San Diego County, they stressed both the need for at least 90 days of in-patient treatment and for an extended period of transition with outpatient treatment while living in a structured sober living facility where continued sobriety is bolstered through ongoing testing, experienced staff and and a community of peers who are also seeking lasting recovery.  Shoreline Sober Living is such a facility. We are extremely grateful for all they have done for our son and us.< /review><Rate>5</Rate>< Time>

<Rate>1<//Rate>< Text>
Please Note- This bad review is base SOLELY on one aspect of this office and nothing else. IF the problem is resolved I would gladly rate this location 5 stars.

I have been coming to this location for almost a year and a half now and have always had excellent care, however the one department that posed a problem a year ago that I haven't had to worry about until now is the referral department. Out of pity, I will not mention the person's name who currently is the root of my problem with this office, and instead I will simply stick to the facts.

On my last visit- April 2nd, 2018 I was told that I would require an MRI and that the request would be submitted as soon as possible as it sometimes takes a while to get approval from Insurance. A week later I was contacted by the MRI office and told to schedule an appointment, which I did for Saturday, April 14th, 2018 (tomorrow).

Yesterday, (Thursday) April 12th, I was contacted by the MRI office and told that did not have authorization yet and that they had spoken to the referral person at this office on Monday, but despite having called back Tuesday, Wednesday and that day Thursday, they had not heard anything back. At that point I called myself and also left 2 messages throughout the day, none of which were returned.

Today (Friday) April 13th, I spoke to the MRI office again and was told that they still had not heard back anything from the referral person, so I call and speak to the receptionist and ask to speak with the referral person directly. I finally get through and he tells me that he did speak with the MRI office on Monday, but ignored all questions about why he did not return their calls afterwards, or mine for that matter. He does tell me he submitted the authorization request on April 3rd , which still should have been plenty of time as my appointment was set for April 13th.

This person has always been dismissive, with a poor attitude when it comes to speaking about his work responsibilities and presents a demeanor befitting of someone who neither cares about his job, nor the people affected by his work. He tells me that he will personally call the insurance company. I ask him to do so and to call me back afterwards.

The MRI office calls me again telling me they have still yet to hear back from this person, I tell them he told me he would call the Insurance company. They then tell me that they discovered the reason the approval was not given was that the authorization request this referral person submitted was not properly filled out and incomplete and that was why they couldn't approve. They would only need to speak with him to complete the form and provide approval. The MRI office tells me they have left yet another message for the referral person, explaining this.

I call the referral person at this location and leave yet another message, also explaining this. It is now 5:13pm, and I have not received a call back from him, nor an explanation, apology, nothing. The MRI office tells me that the insurance authorization has not been changed to approved and therefore I will not get the MRI I have needed and patiently waited over 2 months to have done.

As I have not heard back from the referral person to hear his side of the story, or even if he'll be honest at that point, the underlying questions remain: "Why didn't you return IHS' phone calls?" Whatever the answer may be, when the MRI office called Tuesday, Wednesday, Thursday and Friday and left multiple messages, "Why didn't you return their calls?" "Did you check your messages at all?" "Why didn't you return my calls, or answer my messages?"  Bottom line- there is no excuse good enough.

This referral person obviously has fooled himself into believing the best solution for a mistake that he's made is to simply ignore it, utterly disrespecting anyone else's time. This office would be far better off replacing him, or at the very least reprimanding him so that he better understands the value of his employment and respects the responsibilities of his job.<//Text>

Suffice to say its well over 300lbs. It was done the right way, removed, repaired ,repainted. I had to work for 3 days straight and my wife was going to have to pick up that beast of a truck, which she doesn't like to drive. Instead of picking up my wife so she can drive the F250 home, Marco asked if he could have it dropped off. Not only did my truck show up at home, it was washed and parked where "I" park it! When we called we were clearly told we could smoke both cigars and Hookah. When we arrived there was no outdoor seating and the server said we could not smoke cigars.  It felt like either a bait and switch or an outright lie. There is a nice little cigar/smoke/CBD store next door which had nice prices on Montechristo platinum cigars where I bought one before heading inside sheesha lounge much to my disappointment.

They do have a nice selection of hookah,  bottled water, juice drinks, and comfy lounge couches.  Their Turkish Coffee was actually much milder / weaker than we expected so either it's designed for Starbucks crowds or they don't know how to properly make it.

Prices are reasonable and they'd much better rating if they had not deceived us. Alas, too bad for them.

Lots of locals speaking Arabic which was cool and they knew most of the clients which means they have a dedicated client base which is always a good sign.

Overall a nice place but weak Turkish Coffee and the cigar issue made it a pass for us for future visits.<//Text>

<Review>Being one of the very few places in Costa Mesa that serves tacos and burritos with cabeza and tripa, I really couldn't wait to try this place out. Like other reciews, the parking lot is really small and tight. Luckily for me I came late night and didn't find it too hard to drive and park. I got two cabeza tacos and two tripa tacos. It really fufilled my cravings. The cabeza was soft and tender, lacked some taste but the cilantro and onions and Verde sauce helped. The tripe on the other hand was a bit over cooked and tough to eat but had so much more flavor. If you CANNOT handle spicy , make sure to ask for the sauces on the side! Zamorano is definitely stepping up to the vegan community. Their soyrizo filling is available as a substitution "meat" in any of their tacos, burritos, and tortas. My favorite lunch spot. <Rating>5<//Rating>< text>
Even though parking is very limited the food is so amazing it is worth whatever inconvenience you have to go through to eat here. Seating is limited so large groups will have trouble with seating. They do offer catering (pick up only) to alleviate the situation.

The restaurant is family owned and operated. Their carnies are top notch and tortillas are made fresh to order. Be aware that their salsa does have a little bite to it so if you are sensitive to spicy get it in the side but it is a must try as their salsa is delicious.<//text>

<user_id>110178760489961873417< /user_id><username>hyuk kang<//username>< time>
1424887497235<//time>
< rate>
5< /rate>
< Review>
I tried their al pastor, asada, pollo, and lengua tacos. My favorite was al pastor. It's chunky, crispy outside, with fatty porky meat just hit the spot. With combination of homemade tortilla (yes! i can see their mom just pressing down on that fresh homemade tortilla in their open kitchen) and their kickass spicy sauce gave a perfect street taco flavors. I have to say, Taqueria El Zamorano is my favorite taco spot in OC. Other tacos were good but not as memorable as al pastor. It's family run business with friendly family staff. I also tried their cucumber drink, which was delicious if you want to try other than the usual horchatas. This is one of these spots where I'm afraid to tell people knowing that it maybe too popular, but then I wish their business will grow so that they can sustain this good business.< /Review>
